# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

    25→
    26→// ResourceConfig holds information about all the supported cgroup resource parameters.
    27→type ResourceConfig struct {
    28→	// Memory limit (in bytes).
    29→	Memory *int64
    30→	// CPU set (number of CPUs the cgroup has access to).
    31→	CPUSet cpuset.CPUSet
    32→	// CPU shares (relative weight vs. other containers).
    33→	CPUShares *uint64
    34→	// CPU hardcap limit (in usecs). Allowed cpu time in a given period.
    35→	CPUQuota *int64
    36→	// CPU quota period.
    37→	CPUPeriod *uint64
    38→	// HugePageLimit map from page size (in bytes) to limit (in bytes)
    39→	HugePageLimit map[int64]int64
    40→	// Maximum number of pids
    41→	PidsLimit *int64
    42→	// Unified for cgroup v2
    43→	Unified map[string]string
    44→}
    45→

25-usertext-
I'm building a comprehensive architecture guide for the kubelet container manager subsystem. I need to understand:

1. How the main container manager (containerManagerImpl) integrates with sub-managers:
   - CPU Manager
   - Memory Manager
   - Device Manager
   - DRA Manager
   - Topology Manager
   - QOS Container Manager

2. The cgroup management hierarchy:
   - Linux vs Windows implementations
   - Cgroup v1 vs v2 support
   - System containers

3. Key flow paths:
   - Pod admission flow
   - Container startup flow
   - Resource allocation flow

4. InternalContainerLifecycle implementation

Please search for and explain:
- Main entry points and initialization (how container manager starts up)
- How resourceUpdates channel is used
- Key helper functions for QOS configuration
- The PodAdmitHandler interface and implementations
- How the system container is set up

Use a thorough exploration to understand the full interaction between these components.

    26→// ResourceConfig holds information about all the supported cgroup resource parameters.
    27→type ResourceConfig struct {
    28→	// Memory limit (in bytes).
    29→	Memory *int64
    30→	// CPU set (number of CPUs the cgroup has access to).
    31→	CPUSet cpuset.CPUSet
    32→	// CPU shares (relative weight vs. other containers).
    33→	CPUShares *uint64
    34→	// CPU hardcap limit (in usecs). Allowed cpu time in a given period.
    35→	CPUQuota *int64
    36→	// CPU quota period.
    37→	CPUPeriod *uint64
    38→	// HugePageLimit map from page size (in bytes) to limit (in bytes)
    39→	HugePageLimit map[int64]int64
    40→	// Maximum number of pids
    41→	PidsLimit *int64
    42→	// Unified for cgroup v2
    43→	Unified map[string]string
    44→}

    32→	if i.cpuManager != nil {
    33→		allocatedCPUs := i.cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity(string(pod.UID), container.Name)
    34→		if !allocatedCPUs.IsEmpty() {
    35→			containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetCpus = allocatedCPUs.String()
    36→		}
    37→	}
    38→
    39→	if i.memoryManager != nil {
    40→		numaNodes := i.memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes(logger, pod, container)
    41→		if numaNodes.Len() > 0 {
    42→			var affinity []string
    43→			for _, numaNode := range sets.List(numaNodes) {
    44→				affinity = append(affinity, strconv.Itoa(numaNode))
    45→			}
    46→			containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetMems = strings.Jo

    21→// PodAdmitAttributes is the context for a pod admission decision.
    22→// The member fields of this struct should never be mutated.
    23→type PodAdmitAttributes struct {
    24→	// the pod to evaluate for admission
    25→	Pod *v1.Pod
    26→	// all pods bound to the kubelet excluding the pod being evaluated
    27→	OtherPods []*v1.Pod
    28→}
    29→
    30→// PodAdmitResult provides the result of a pod admission decision.
    31→type PodAdmitResult struct {
    32→	// if true, the pod should be admitted.
    33→	Admit bool
    34→	// a brief single-word reason why the pod could not be admitted.
    35→	Reason string
    36→	// a brief message explaining why the pod could not be admitted.
    37→	Message string
    38→}
    39→
    40→// PodAdmitHandler is notified during pod admission.
    41→type PodAdmitHandler interface {
    42→	// Admit evaluates if a pod can be admitted.
    43→	Admit(attrs *PodAdmitAttributes) PodAdmitResult
    44→}

    34→// cgroupV1impl implements the CgroupManager interface
    35→// for cgroup v1.
    36→// It's a stateless object which can be used to
    37→// update, create or delete any number of cgroups
    38→// It relies on runc/libcontainer cgroup managers.
    39→type cgroupV1impl struct {
    40→	cgroupCommon
    41→}
    42→
    43→func NewCgroupV1Manager(logger klog.Logger, cs *CgroupSubsystems, cgroupDriver string) CgroupManager {
    44→	return &cgroupV1impl{
    45→		cgroupCommon: newCgroupCommon(logger, cs, cgroupDriver),
    46→	}

# Kubelet Container Manager Subsystem: Architecture Guide

## Executive Summary

The kubelet container manager is the subsystem responsible for:
- Managing container resource allocation and enforcement across the node
- Enforcing Kubernetes QoS (Quality of Service) tiers via cgroup hierarchies
- Coordinating topology-aware resource allocation (CPU affinity, NUMA memory alignment)
- Extending resource management through device plugins and dynamic resource allocation
- Maintaining system stability through resource isolation and admission control

This subsystem sits between the Kubernetes API layer (pod specifications) and the container runtime (cgroups and Linux kernel resource controls).

---

## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose and Scope

The container manager subsystem is responsible for translating Kubernetes pod and container resource specifications into enforceable OS-level resource constraints. It provides:

1. **Resource Isolation**: Prevents pods from exceeding allocated resources
2. **QoS Enforcement**: Implements Kubernetes QoS tiers (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) with distinct CPU and memory behavior
3. **Topology Optimization**: Aligns container resources to hardware topology (NUMA nodes) for optimal performance
4. **Device Management**: Brokers extended resources (GPUs, accelerators) reported by device plugins
5. **Admission Control**: Rejects pods that violate topology constraints before container creation
6. **Node Accounting**: Tracks system resource consumption and ensures node allocatable is respected

### Subsystem Boundaries

**Upstream Dependencies** (What feeds into this subsystem):
- **Pod Specification** (`v1.Pod`): CPU/memory requests and limits, QoS class, device plugin r
... (truncated)

Builds container map from runtime\n2. Initializes DRA Manager\n3. Starts CPU Manager with active pods callback\n4. Starts Memory Manager\n5. Sets up system containers (kernel tuning, OOM scoring)\n6. CGROUP MANAGEMENT HIERARCHY\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` (manager selection)\n\n#### **Cgroup v1 Implementation**\n- **File:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`\n- **Manager:** `cgroupV1impl`\n- **Key Constants:**\n  ```go\n  const cgroupv1MemLimitFile string = \"memory.limit_in_bytes\"\n  ```\n- **Features:**\n  - Unified hierarchy with better resource coordination\n  - Enhanced memory.min/memory.high for memory QoS\n  - Kernel 5.8+ required for root cpu.stat\n\n#### **Cgroup Hierarchy Structure:**\n\n```\n/kubepods (cgroupRoot / defaultNodeAllocatableCgroupName)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 kubepods.slice (systemd format)\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 /guaranteed (Guaranteed QoS pods)\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 /burstable (Burstable QoS pods)\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 pod-{UID} (pod-level cgroups)\n  \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 container1\n  \u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 container2\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 /besteffort (BestEffort QoS pods)\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 pod-{UID}\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 /system (system containers)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 /kubelet (kubelet process cgroup)\n```\n\n#### **System Containers:**\n\n- **System Container** (`SystemCgroupsName`): Runs non-containerized processes\n- **Kubelet Container** (`KubeletCgroupsName`): Confines kubelet process with OOM score adjustment\n- **Periodic Enforcement:** Every 5 minutes to move escaped processes back\n\n---\n\n### 4. KEY FLOW PATHS\n\n#### **A. Pod Admission Flow**\n\n**Interface:** `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler` (in `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/interfaces.go`)\n\n```go\ntype PodAdmitHandler interface {\n    Admit(attrs *PodAdmitAttributes) PodAdmitResult\n}\n\ntype PodAdmitAttributes struct {\n    Pod *v1.Pod\n    OtherPods []*v1.Pod\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation:** Topology Manager implements this interface\n\n**Flow:**\n1. Kubelet calls `Admit()` during pod acceptance phase\n2. **Topology Manager** (`GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns it):\n   - Collects topology hints from all hint providers (CPU, Memory, Device managers)\n   - Evaluates if topology alignment is possible\n   - Returns `PodAdmitResult` with Accept/Reject decision\n3. If admitted, moves to container startup\n4. If rejected, pod is rejected with `TopologyAffinityError`\n\n#### **B. Container Startup Flow**\n\n**Interface:** `InternalContainerLifecycle` (in `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Implementation:**\n\n```go\ntype internalContainerLifecycleImpl struct {\n    cpuManager      cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager   memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager topologymanager.Manager\n}\n\nfunc (i *internalContainerLifecycleImpl) PreCreateContainer(\n    logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, \n    containerConfig *runtimeapi.ContainerConfig) error\nfunc (i *internalContainerLifecycleImpl) PreStartContainer(\n    logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, \n    containerID string) error\nfunc (i *internalContainerLifecycleImpl) PostStopContainer(\n    logger klog.Logger, containerID string) error\n```\n\n**Phases:**\n\n1. **PreCreateContainer** (`internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`):\n   - CPU Manager: Gets CPU affinity from `GetCPUAffinity()` \u2192 sets `cpusetCpus`\n   - Memory Manager: Gets NUMA nodes \u2192 sets `cpusetMems`\n   - Topology Manager: Not called at this stage\n\n2. **PreStartContainer**:\n   - CPU Manager: `AddContainer()` - records container-to-CPU mapping\n   - Memory Manager: `AddContainer()` - records container-to-memory mapping\n   - Topology Manager: `AddContainer()` - tracks container lifecycle\n\n3. **PostStopContainer**:\n   - Topology Manager: `RemoveContainer()` - cleans up affinity tracking\n   - Other managers handle their own cleanup\n\n#### **C. Resource Allocation Flow**\n\n**Location:** `qos_container_manager_linux.go` (lines 316-392, `UpdateCgroups()` method)\n\n**Periodic Update Interval:** 1 minute (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. **CPU Shares Calculation** (`setCPUCgroupConfig()`):\n   - Sums CPU requests from all active Burstable pods\n   - Best Effort always gets `MinShares` (2)\n   - Burstable gets calculated shares: `MilliCPUToShares(burstablePodCPURequest)`\n\n2. **Memory Limits** (`setMemoryReserve()`):\n   - Only if QOSReserved feature enabled\n   - Calculates: `burstableLimit = allocatable - (guaranteed * percentReserve / 100)`\n   - Retries if memory usage exceeds limit\n\n3. **Memory QoS** (`setMemoryQoS()` for cgroup v2):\n   - Sets `memory.min` for burstable and guaranteed tiers\n   - Only if MemoryQoS feature enabled and cgroup v2\n\n4. **Updates Applied:**\n   - Calls `cgroupManager.Update()` for each QoS tier\n   - Huge pages set as unbounded\n\n---\n\n### 5. THE resourceUpdates CHANNEL SYSTEM\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/resourceupdates/updates.go`\n\n**Data Structure:**\n```go\ntype Update struct {\n    PodUIDs []string  // Pod UIDs that need status update\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation Details** (container_manager_linux.go, lines 358-389):\n\n1. **Channel Creation:**\n   - Single buffered channel with capacity 10\n   - Created in `NewContainerManager()`\n\n2. **Fan-In Pattern:**\n   ```go\n   sources := map[string]<-chan resourceupdates.Update{}\n   if cm.deviceManager != nil {\n       sources[\"deviceManager\"] = cm.deviceManager.Updates()\n   }\n   if utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.DynamicResourceAllocation) \n       && cm.draManager != nil {\n       sources[\"draManager\"] = cm.draManager.Updates()\n   }\n   \n   // Each source gets a goroutine to forward updates\n   for name, ch := range sources {\n       wg.Add(1)\n       go func(name string, c <-chan resourceupdates.Update) {\n           defer wg.Done()\n           for v := range c {\n               logger.V(4).Info(\"Container Manager: forwarding resource update\", \n                   \"source\", name, \"pods\", v.PodUIDs)\n               cm.resourceUpdates <- v\n           }\n       }(name, ch)\n   }\n   \n   // Close channel when all sources are done\n   go func() {\n       wg.Wait()\n       close(cm.resourceUpdates)\n   }()\n   ```\n\n3. **Usage:**\n   - Exposed via `Updates()` method returning `<-chan resourceupdates.Update`\n   - Kubelet's main sync loop consumes updates to reconcile pod status\n   - Triggered when device health changes or DRA resources become unavailable\n\n---\n\n### 6. QOS CONFIGURATION HELPER FUNCTIONS\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go`\n\n**Key Constants:**\n```go\nconst (\n    MinShares = 2          // Minimum CPU shares (kernel default for zero)\n    MaxShares = 262144     // Maximum CPU shares\n    SharesPerCPU  = 1024   // Shares equivalent to 1 full CPU\n    MilliCPUToCPU = 1000   // Conversion factor\n    QuotaPeriod = 100000   // Default CFS period (100ms in microseconds)\n    MinQuotaPeriod = 1000  // Minimum CFS period (1ms)\n    MinMilliCPULimit = 10  // Minimum milliCPU limit\n)\n```\n\n**Key Functions:**\n\n1. **MilliCPUToShares(milliCPU int64) uint64**\n   - Converts milliCPU to CPU shares for weighted scheduling\n   - Formula: `(milliCPU * SharesPerCPU) / MilliCPUToCPU`\n   - Clamps to `MinShares`-`MaxShares` range\n   - Zero milliCPU returns `MinShares`\n\n2. **MilliCPUToQuota(milliCPU, period int64) int64**\n   - Converts milliCPU to CFS quota (hard limit)\n   - Formula: `(milliCPU * period) / MilliCPUToCPU`\n   - Respects `CPUCFSQuotaPeriod` feature gate\n   - Minimum quota is `MinQuotaPeriod` (1ms)\n\n3. **HugePageLimits(resourceList v1.ResourceList) map[int64]int64**\n   - Extracts huge page sizes from resource list\n   - Maps size to cumulative limit\n\n4. **ResourceConfigForPod(...) *ResourceConfig**\n   - Calculates resource config for pod cgroup creation\n   - Considers:\n     - Pod CPU/memory requests and limits\n     - EnforceCPULimits flag\n     - MemoryQoS feature gate\n     - PodLevelResources feature gate\n\n---\n\n### 7. PODADMITHANDLER INTERFACE AND IMPLEMENTATIONS\n\n**Primary Implementation:** Topology Manager\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`\n\n**Method:** `Admit(attrs *lifecycle.PodAdmitAttributes) lifecycle.PodAdmitResult`\n\n**Admission Process:**\n\n1. **Scope Determination:** Pod-scoped vs Container-scoped\n2. **Hint Collection:**\n   - Calls `GetTopologyHints()` on all registered hint providers\n   - Providers: Device Manager, CPU Manager, Memory Manager\n3. **Hint Aggregation:**\n   - Merges hints based on policy (none, best-effort, restricted)\n   - Checks feasibility\n4. **Decision:**\n   - Returns `PodAdmitResult{Admit: true/false, Reason, Message}`\n   - `TopologyAffinityError` type for rejections\n\n**Other Handlers:**\n- Device Manager may implement its own handlers for resource validation\n- DRA Manager implements pod preparation handlers (not admission, but related)\n\n---\n\n### 8. SYSTEM CONTAINER SETUP\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (lines 504-584)\n\n**Process: `setupNode()`**\n\n1. **System Requirements Validation:**\n   - Checks kernel tunables (VM overcommit, panic settings, etc.)\n   - Validates CPU hardcapping support\n\n2. **QOS Container Setup:**\n   - Creates top-level QoS containers if `CgroupsPerQOS` enabled\n   - Creates for Burstable and BestEffort (Guaranteed is root)\n   - Starts QOS manager with periodic updates (1-minute interval)\n\n3. **Node Allocatable Enforcement:**\n   - Creates node allocatable cgroup (`kubepods`)\n   - Enforces resource limits on this cgroup\n   - Handles memory overage with retries\n\n4. **System Containers:**\n   ```go\n   if cm.SystemCgroupsName != \"\" {\n       // Create system container for non-containerized processes\n       cont.ensureStateFunc = func(manager cgroups.Manager) error {\n           return ensureSystemCgroups(logger, \"/\", manager)\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Kubelet Container:**\n   - Moves kubelet process into configured cgroup\n   - Applies OOM score adjustment\n   - If no explicit cgroup, periodic task finds and tracks kubelet's cgroup\n\n6. **Periodic Tasks:**\n   - **For system containers:** Every 1 minute - ensure state (move processes)\n   - **For kubelet location:** Every 5 minutes - update kubelet cgroup location\n\n---\n\n### 9. createManager(containerName string) (cgroups.Manager, error) {\n   436\u2192\tcg := &cgroups.Cgroup{\n   437\u2192\t\tParent: \"/\",\n   438\u2192\t\tName:   containerName,\n   439\u2192\t\tResources: 447\u2192\n   448\u2192type KernelTunableBehavior string\n   449\u2192\n   450\u2192const (\n   451\u2192\tKernelTunableWarn   KernelTunableBehavior = \"warn\"\n   452\u2192\tKernelTunableError are set as expected\n   457\u2192// depending upon the specified option, it will either warn, error, or modify the kernel tunable flags\n   458\u2192func setupKernelTunables(logger klog.Logger, option KernelTunableBehavior) error {\n   459\u2192\tdesiredState := map[string]int{\n   460\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.VMOvercommitMemory: utilsysctl.VMOvercommitMemoryAlways,\n   461\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.VMPanicOnOOM:       utilsysctl.VMPanicOnOOMInvokeOOMKiller,\n   462\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.KernelPanic:        utilsysctl.KernelPanicRebootTimeout,\n   463\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.KernelPanicOnOops:  utilsysctl.KernelPanicOnOopsAlways,\n   464\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.RootMaxKeys:        utilsysctl.RootMaxKeysSetting,\n   465\u2192\t\tutilsysctl.RootMaxBytes:       utilsysctl.RootMaxBytesSetting,\n   466\u2192\t}\n   467\u2192\n   468\u2192\tsysctl := utilsysctl.New()\n   469\u2192\n   470\u2192\terrList := []error{}\n   471\u2192\tfor flag, expectedValue := range desiredState {\n   472\u2192\t\tval, err := sysctl.GetSysctl(flag)\n   473\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   474\u2192\t\t\terrList = append(errList, err)\n   475\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   476\u2192\t\t}\n   477\u2192\t\tif val == expectedValue {\n   478\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   479\u2192\t\t}\n   480\u2192\n   481\u2192\t\tswitch option {\n   482\u2192\t\tcase KernelTunableError:\n   483\u2192\t\t\terrList = append(errList, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid kernel flag: %v, expected value: %v, actual value: %v\", flag, expectedValue, val))\n   484\u2192\t\tcase KernelTunableWarn:\n   485\u2192\t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Invalid kernel flag\", \"flag\", flag, \"expectedValue\", expectedValue, \"actualValue\", val)\n   486\u2192\t\tcase KernelTunableModify:\n   487\u2192\t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Updating kernel flag\", \"flag\", flag, \"expectedValue\", expectedValue, \"actualValue\", val)\n   488\u2192\t\t\terr = sysctl.SetSysctl(flag, expectedValue)\n   489\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   490\u2192\t\t\t\tif inuserns.RunningInUserNS() {\n   491\u2192\t\t\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.KubeletInUserNamespace) {\n   492\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Updating kernel flag failed (running in UserNS, ignoring)\", \"flag\", flag, \"err\", err)\n   493\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   494\u2192\t\t\t\t\t}\n   495\u2192\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Updating kernel flag failed (Hint: enable KubeletInUserNamespace feature flag to ignore the error)\", \"flag\", flag)\n   496\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   497\u2192\t\t\t\terrList = append(errList, err)\n   498\u2192\t\t\t}\n   499\u2192\t\t}\n   500\u2192\t}\n   501\u2192\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errList)\n   502\u2192}\n   503\u2192\n 835\u2192}\n   836\u2192\n   837\u2192// getContainer returns the cgroup associated with the specified pid.\n   838\u2192// It enforces a unified hierarchy for memory and cpu cgroups.\n   839\u2192// On systemd environments, it uses the name=systemd cgroup for the specified pid.\n   840\u2192func getContainer(logger klog.Logger, pid int) (string, error) {\n   841\u2192\tcgs, err := cgroups.ParseCgroupFile(fmt.Sprintf(\"/proc/%d/cgroup\", pid))\n   842\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   843\u2192\t\treturn \"\", err\n   844\u2192\t}\n   845\u2192\n   846\u2192\tif 851\u2192\t\treturn c, nil\n   852\u2192\t}\n   853\u2192\n   854\u2192\tcpu, found := cgs[\"cpu\"]\n   855\u2192\tif !found {\n   856\u2192\t\treturn \"\", cgroups.NewNotFoundError(\"cpu\")\n   857\u2192\t}\n   858\u2192\tmemory, found := cgs[\"memory\"]\n   859\u2192\tif !found {\n   860\u2192\t\treturn \"\", cgroups.NewNotFoundError(\"memory\")\n   861\u2192\t}\n   862\u2192\n   863\u2192\t// since we use this container for accounting, we need to ensure its a unified hierarchy.\n   864\u2192\tif cpu != memory {\n   865\u2192\t\treturn \"\", fmt.Errorf(\"cpu and memory cgroup hierarchy not unified.  cpu: %s, memory: %s\", cpu, memory)\n   866\u2192\t}\n   867\u2192\n   868\u2192\t// on systemd, every pid is in a unified cgroup hierarchy (name=systemd as seen in systemd-cgls)\n   869\u2192\t// cpu and memory accounting is off by default, users may choose to enable it per unit or globally.\n   870\u2192\t// users could enable CPU and memory accounting globally via /etc/systemd/system.conf (DefaultCPUAccounting=true DefaultMemoryAccounting=true).\n   871\u2192\t// users could also enable CPU and memory accounting per unit via CPUAccounting=true and MemoryAccounting=true\n   872\u2192\t// we only warn if accounting is not enabled for CPU or memory so as to not break local development flows where kubelet is launched in a terminal.\n   873\u2192\t// for example, the cgroup for the user session will be something like /user.slice/user-X.slice/session-X.scope, but the cpu and memory\n   874\u2192\t// cgroup will be the closest ancestor where accounting is performed (most likely /) on systems that launch docker containers.\n   875\u2192\t// as a result, on those systems, you will not get cpu or memory accounting statistics for kubelet.\n   876\u2192\t// in addition, you would not get memory or cpu accounting for the runtime unless accounting was enabled on its unit (or globally).\n   877\u2192\tif systemd, found :=  887\u2192\treturn cpu, nil\n   888\u2192}\n   889\u2192\n   890\u2192// Ensures the system container is created and all non-kernel threads and process 1\n   891\u2192// without a container are moved and create priority inversions.\n   895\u2192func ensureSystemCgroups(logger klog.Logger, rootCgroupPath string, manager cgroups.Manager) error {\n   896\u2192\t// Move non-kernel PIDs to the system Input
{
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Subsystem: Architecture Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is the subsystem responsible for:\n- Managing container resource allocation and enforcement across the node\n- Enforcing Kubernetes QoS (Quality of Service) tiers via cgroup hierarchies\n- Coordinating topology-aware resource allocation (CPU affinity, NUMA memory alignment)\n- Extending resource management through device plugins and dynamic resource allocation\n- Maintaining system stability through resource isolation and admission control\n\nThis subsystem sits between the Kubernetes API layer (pod specifications) and the container runtime (cgroups and Linux kernel resource controls).\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose and Scope\n\nThe container manager subsystem is responsible for translating Kubernetes pod and container resource specifications into enforceable OS-level resource constraints. It provides:\n\n1. **Resource Isolation**: Prevents pods from exceeding allocated resources\n2. **QoS Enforcement**: Implements Kubernetes QoS tiers (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) with distinct CPU and memory behavior\n3. **Topology Optimization**: Aligns container resources to hardware topology (NUMA nodes) for optimal performance\n4. **Device Management**: Brokers extended resources (GPUs, accelerators) reported by device plugins\n5. **Admission Control**: Rejects pods that violate topology constraints before container creation\n6. **Node Accounting**: Tracks system resource consumption and ensures node allocatable is respected\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies** (What feeds into this subsystem):\n- **Pod Specification** (`v1.Pod`): CPU/memory requests and limits, QoS class, device plugin resource requests\n- **Node Specification** (`v1.Node`): Capacity, allocatable, extended resource counts\n- **Runtime Service** (`internalapi.RuntimeService`): Container startup notifications, actual container limits\n- **Active Pods Callback** (`ActivePodsFunc`): Current running pods for recalculation\n- **Plugin Manager**: Device plugin registration and health status\n\n**Downstream Consumers** (What this subsystem affects):\n- **Container Runtime** (CRI): Container execution with configured cpuset, memory limits via `RunContainerOptions`\n- **Cgroup Filesystem**: Direct manipulation via cgroup manager for resource limits\n- **Kubelet Status Module**: Pod resource status via `PodResources` API and allocated resources\n- **Scheduler Framework**: Topology hints inform scheduler pod placement decisions\n- **Kubelet Metrics**: CPU/memory usage from cAdvisor integration\n\n### Architectural Constraints\n\n- **Per-Node Scope**: Operates only on the local node; no inter-node coordination\n- **Immutable Pod QoS**: QoS class is determined once during pod creation based on requests/limits, not updated\n- **Best-Effort Reconciliation**: Periodic (1-minute) updates ensure desired vs. actual state; no per-container hooks\n- **Cgroup Version Coupling**: Behavior differs significantly between cgroup v1 and v2 with separate code paths\n- **Linux-Primary Design**: Most functionality (CPU/memory managers, QOS tiers) is Linux-only; Windows is minimal\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Central Orchestrator: containerManagerImpl\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (lines 100-140)\n\nThe `containerManagerImpl` struct is the central hub managing lifecycle and delegation:\n\n```go\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    sync.RWMutex\n    // Infrastructure\n    cadvisorInterface cadvisor.Interface\n    cgroupManager CgroupManager\n    nodeInfo *v1.Node\n    systemContainers []*systemContainer\n\n    // Configuration\n    NodeConfig\n    subsystems *CgroupSubsystems\n    cgroupRoot CgroupName\n\n    // State and Capacity\n    capacity v1.ResourceList\n    internalCapacity v1.ResourceList\n\n    // Sub-managers for resource coordination\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    deviceManager devicemanager.Manager\n    cpuManager cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager topologymanager.Manager\n    draManager *dra.Manager\n\n    // Event distribution\n    recorder record.EventRecorder\n    resourceUpdates chan resourceupdates.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n1. Initialize and start all sub-managers during node setup\n2. Provide facade methods for capacity reporting (`GetCapacity`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation`)\n3. Distribute admission decisions via topology manager\n4. Route dynamic resource changes to consumers via `resourceUpdates` channel\n5. Implement `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks for resource pre-configuration\n\n### 2.2 Sub-Manager Components\n\n#### A. CPU Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: CPU affinity assignment and exclusive CPU allocation\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Load existing allocations from checkpoint\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Assign CPUs and record decision\n- `GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName) cpuset.CPUSet`: Return CPU assignment\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName) cpuset.CPUSet`: Query for PodResources API\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No assignment, container uses all CPUs\n- `static`: Bind exclusive containers to specific CPUs (deterministic allocation from reserved CPUs)\n- Both policies respect `reserved` CPUs (system, kube-reserved) and isolated CPUs (via topology manager hints)\n\n**Failure Mode**:\n- If static policy cannot find contiguous CPU set for exclusive container \u2192 returns error\n- Pod stays pending until CPUs available or request modified\n\n#### B. Memory Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: NUMA-aware memory allocation and huge page configuration\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Detect NUMA topology and restore allocations\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Allocate NUMA nodes\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA hints to topology manager\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No NUMA affinity, container can access all memory\n- `static`: Bind containers to specific NUMA nodes\n- `best-effort`: Allocate from single NUMA node if possible, else multi-node\n\n**State Persistence**: Checkpoint file at `<kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state`\n\n#### C. Topology Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Coordinate topology affinity across all hint providers; enforce policies during pod admission\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Admit(attrs *lifecycle.PodAdmitAttributes) lifecycle.PodAdmitResult`: Gating function for pod acceptance\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container) []NUMATopologyHint`: Query hint providers for alignment options\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Record topology assignment\n- `RemoveContainer(containerID)`: Clean up tracking\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No enforcement (all pods admitted)\n- `best-effort`: Prefers aligned topology but admits misaligned pods\n- `restricted`: Rejects misaligned pods (only admits if all hints agree on NUMA nodes)\n- `single-numa-node`: All containers in pod must fit on single NUMA node\n\n**Scope**:\n- `pod`: Aggregate hints across all containers, one decision per pod\n- `container`: Each container evaluated independently\n\n**Admission Decision Flow**:\n```\nPod Arrival\n  \u2193\nTopology Manager.Admit()\n  \u251c\u2500 Query CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500 Query Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500 Query Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500 Aggregate hints using policy\n  \u251c\u2500 Check if feasible combination exists\n  \u2514\u2500 Return Accept or Reject\n```\n\n#### D. Device Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage extended resources (GPUs, accelerators); broker device plugin allocation\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Discover devices and watch plugin registration endpoints\n- `Allocate(pod, container, requests): error`: Allocate devices via plugin Allocate RPC\n- `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity(): (capacity, allocatable, inactive)`: Report resource counts\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container): []hints`: Provide NUMA topology hints if devices are NUMA-aware\n- `Updates() <-chan resourceupdates.Update`: Broadcast device health changes\n\n**Device Plugin Integration**:\n- Uses Unix socket discovery (`/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`)\n- Implements both v1beta1 (legacy) and v1 (current) plugin APIs\n- Tracks allocation state per pod for recovery on restart\n\n**State Persistence**: Device allocation checkpoint at `<kubelet-root>/device-plugin-state`\n\n#### E. Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage ResourceClaims (Kubernetes 1.26+); prepare and unprepare dynamic resources\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `PrepareDynamicResources(ctx, pod)`: Claim resources from ResourceClaim specs\n- `UnprepareDynamicResources(ctx, pod)`: Release claimed resources\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)`: Provide topology hints based on claimed resources\n- `Updates() <-chan resourceupdates.Update`: Broadcast unavailable claims\n\n**Resource Claim Lifecycle**:\n```\nPod with ResourceClaim Spec\n  \u2193\nPrepareDynamicResources()\n  \u251c\u2500 Call resource driver's Prepare RPC\n  \u251c\u2500 Wait for ResourceClaim status.AllocationResult\n  \u251c\u2500 Record claim allocation\n  \u2514\u2500 Return CDI device specs to container runtime\n  \u2193\nContainer Created with CDI devices\n  \u2193\nPod Deletion\n  \u2193\nUnprepareDynamicResources()\n  \u251c\u2500 Call resource driver's Unprepare RPC\n  \u2514\u2500 Clean up claim state\n```\n\n**Failure Handling**: If claim becomes unavailable mid-pod-life, sends update \u2192 kubelet can evict pod\n\n#### F. QoS Container Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage top-level QoS-tier cgroups and enforce per-tier resource policies\n\n**QoS Tiers**:\n- **Guaranteed**: Pods with requests == limits; highest priority; full CPU access when not contested\n- **Burstable**: Pods with requests but no limits; medium priority; CPU shares proportional to requests\n- **BestEffort**: Pods with neither requests nor limits; lowest priority; killed first under pressure\n\n**Resource Configuration**:\n- **CPU Shares**:\n  - Guaranteed: Unlimited (no shares limit)\n  - Burstable: Sum of all pod requests converted via `MilliCPUToShares()`: `(milliCPU * 1024) / 1000` with `Min=2, Max=262144`\n  - BestEffort: 2 shares (kernel minimum)\n- **Memory**: Applied per-pod under QoS tier parent\n- **Memory QoS** (cgroup v2 only):\n  - Sets `memory.min` for burstable and guaranteed tiers\n  - Protects these pods from memory pressure\n\n**Periodic Update**: Every 60 seconds (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`) via `UpdateQOSCgroups()`\n\n**CPU Quota Override**: If `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` feature enabled and pod has exclusive CPUs, CPU limits (quota) disabled\n\n#### G. Pod Container Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Create and manage pod-level cgroups within QoS tiers\n\n**Hierarchy**:\n```\nQoSContainer (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Pod Cgroup (kubepods.burstable.podXXX)\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Container cgroup (created by runtime with cpuset, memory)\n```\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `EnsureExists(pod)`: Create pod cgroup with CPU/memory config\n- `GetPodContainerName(pod)`: Compute cgroup name from QoS class\n- `Destroy(podCgroupName)`: Remove pod cgroup\n- `IsPodCgroup(cgroupfsName): (bool, types.UID)`: Check if cgroupfs path is a pod\n\n**Pod Cgroup Configuration** (via `ResourceConfigForPod()`):\n- CPU shares from pod requests, adjusted for QoS tier\n- Memory limit = pod requests (or limits if present)\n- CPU quota only if `enforceCPULimits=true` (can disable for exclusive CPUs)\n- Huge page limits from pod resource specs\n\n#### H. Cgroup Manager (Linux)\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` (dispatcher), `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Abstract cgroup filesystem or systemd interface for Create/Update/Destroy operations\n\n**Implementation Options**:\n- **cgroupv1impl**: Direct cgroup filesystem manipulation (`/sys/fs/cgroup/...`)\n- **cgroupv2impl**: Unified cgroup v2 hierarchy with single write path\n- **Systemd Driver**: Uses systemd unit files (slices) instead of direct filesystem\n\n**Interface** (from `types.go`):\n```go\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Update(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Exists(name CgroupName) bool\n    Name(name CgroupName) string        // Internal \u2192 cgroupfs\n    Pids(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) []int\n    MemoryUsage(name CgroupName) (int64, error)\n    GetCgroupConfig(name CgroupName, resource v1.ResourceName) (*ResourceConfig, error)\n    Version() int                        // 1 or 2\n}\n```\n\n**Key Resource Parameters** (ResourceConfig):\n- `Memory`: Limit in bytes (memory.limit_in_bytes or memory.max)\n- `CPUSet`: CPUs accessible (cpuset.cpus)\n- `CPUShares`: CPU relative weight (cpu.shares)\n- `CPUQuota`: Hard CPU limit in microseconds (cpu.cfs_quota_us)\n- `PidsLimit`: Max process count (pids.max)\n- `Unified`: cgroup v2-only settings (memory.min, memory.high, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: End-to-End Control Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization\n\n**Entry Point**: `NewContainerManager()` in `container_manager_linux.go` (lines 207-392)\n\n```\nNewContainerManager()\n  \u251c\u2500 1. Detect mounted subsystems\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 GetCgroupSubsystems() \u2192 CgroupSubsystems{cpu, memory, cpuset, ...}\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. Validate requirements\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Ensure cpu and memory subsystems mounted\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Log deprecation warning if cgroup v1 detected\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 3. Create cgroup manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewCgroupManager(cgroupDriver, cgroupVersion) \u2192 cgroupV1impl or cgroupV2impl\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 4. Initialize topology manager (policy enforcement hub)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewTopologyManager(policy, scope, machineInfo)\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 machineInfo from cAdvisor (NUMA topology)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 5. Initialize device manager (with topology hints)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewManagerImpl(topologyHints=topologyManager)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 6. Initialize CPU manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewManager(cpuPolicy, nodeConfig.ReservedSystemCPUs)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 7. Initialize memory manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewManager(memoryPolicy, nodeConfig.MemoryManagerReservedMemory)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 8. Initialize DRA manager (if feature enabled)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 NewManager(kubeClient, nodeConfig.NodeName)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 9. Register hint providers with topology manager\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 topologyManager.AddHintProvider(cpuManager)\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 topologyManager.AddHintProvider(memoryManager)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 topologyManager.AddHintProvider(deviceManager)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 10. Initialize QoS container manager\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 NewQOSContainerManager(cgroupManager, cgroupsPerQOS)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 11. Create resource updates channel\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 resourceUpdates = make(chan resourceupdates.Update, 10)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 12. Fan-in resource update streams (concurrent goroutines)\n         \u251c\u2500 deviceManager.Updates() \u2192 resourceUpdates\n         \u2514\u2500 draManager.Updates() \u2192 resourceUpdates\n```\n\n**Key Evidence**:\n- Lines 249-251: Topology manager initialized before managers that use it\n- Lines 272-280: Device and CPU managers added as hint providers\n- Lines 358-389: Fan-in pattern for resource updates with error handling per source\n\n### 3.2 Node Startup Flow\n\n**Entry Point**: `Start()` in `container_manager_linux.go` (lines 615-710)\n\nThis is called once per node lifecycle when kubelet starts:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl.Start(ctx, node, activePodsFunc, getNodeFunc, ...)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 1. Build existing container map from runtime\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 containerMap := buildContainerMap(pod, containers from cgroups)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. Initialize DRA manager with existing pods\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 draManager.Start(activePodsFunc) for recovery\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 3. Start CPU manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 cpuManager.Start(activePodsFunc)\n  \u2502        \u251c\u2500 Load checkpoint from <kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Reconcile allocations, move escaped processes back to cpusets\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 4. Start memory manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 memoryManager.Start(activePodsFunc)\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Similar checkpoint loading and reconciliation\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 5. Setup node (cgroup initialization and enforcement)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 setupNode() [covered below]\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 6. Start device manager\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 deviceManager.Start(pod-based resource cleanup)\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Watch /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/ for plugin registration\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 7. Start health checkers for plugins\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 GetHealthCheckers() \u2192 kubelet integrates with systemd watchdog\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 8. Start periodic tasks\n       \u251c\u2500 cpu reconciliation (ongoing)\n       \u251c\u2500 memory reconciliation (ongoing)\n       \u251c\u2500 QoS resource updates (60s interval)\n       \u2514\u2500 System container enforcement (60s interval)\n```\n\n**Critical Phase: setupNode()** (lines 504-584):\n\n```\nsetupNode()\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 1. Kernel tuning\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Check kernel.sysrq allowed\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Check vm.overcommit_memory\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Warn if protection defaults differ\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. QoS tier cgroup creation (if CgroupsPerQOS=true)\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Create /kubepods/burstable cgroup\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Create /kubepods/besteffort cgroup\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Start QoS manager for periodic tier-level resource updates\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 3. Create system container\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Create systemCgroup if SystemCgroupsName specified\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Periodically (60s) move non-pod processes there\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Prevent processes from escaping QoS hierarchy\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 4. Create kubelet container\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Allocate own cgroup if KubeletCgroupsName specified\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Apply OOM score adjustment (KubeletOOMScoreAdj)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Move kubelet process into cgroup (or track its cgroup)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 5. Enforce node allocatable\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Create root pod cgroup (/kubepods)\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Apply resource limits (CPU shares, memory)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Enforce with retries if memory oversubscribed\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 6. Return Status with any soft requirement violations\n       \u2514\u2500 e.g., \"cgroup v1 is deprecated, use cgroup v2\"\n```\n\n**File Evidence**:\n- Lines 89-98: System container creation with `newSystemCgroups()`\n- Lines 512-530: Node allocatable cgroup creation and enforcement\n- Lines 532-558: System and kubelet container setup with periodic tasks\n- Lines 563-584: Resource reservation enforcement\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission Flow (Pre-Container Creation)\n\n**Entry Point**: `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns the topology manager's Admit method\n\nCalled by kubelet's pod admission controller when a new pod arrives:\n\n```\nKubelet receives Pod Spec\n  \u2193\nPod Admission Controller\n  \u251c\u2500 Call handlers from containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 \u2192 Returns topology manager's Admit(PodAdmitAttributes)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Topology Manager.Admit(attrs) [topologymanager.go]\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500 1. Determine scope (pod-scoped or container-scoped)\n      \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Based on policy configuration\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500 2. Collect topology hints\n      \u2502    \u251c\u2500 For each container in pod:\n      \u2502    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      \u2502    \u2502   \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Returns possible NUMA node sets for CPU allocation\n      \u2502    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      \u2502    \u2502   \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Returns compatible NUMA nodes for memory\n      \u2502    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      \u2502    \u2502      \u2514\u2500 Returns NUMA locality for allocated devices\n      \u2502    \u2502\n      \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Collect hints per resource type (cpus, memory, devices, ...)\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500 3. Apply policy logic\n      \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Policy: none\n      \u2502    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Accept all (no topology enforcement)\n      \u2502    \u2502\n      \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Policy: best-effort\n      \u2502    \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Find intersection of all hint sets\n      \u2502    \u2502  \u251c\u2500 If no intersection \u2192 Accept anyway (prefer aligned, allow misaligned)\n      \u2502    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Record preferred affinity\n      \u2502    \u2502\n      \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Policy: restricted\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Find intersection of all hint sets\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500 If no intersection \u2192 Reject pod (TopologyAffinityError)\n      \u2502       \u2514\u2500 Only accept if all hints agree on NUMA assignment\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500 4. Return decision\n      \u2502    \u251c\u2500 Accept=true \u2192 Pod proceeds to scheduling\n      \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Accept=false, Reason=\"TopologyAffinityError\" \u2192 Pod rejected\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500 5. Record admission decision in topology manager state\n           \u2514\u2500 For later reference during actual container creation\n```\n\n**Topology Manager Implementation Evidence**:\n- File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`\n- Hint collection: Iterates hint providers via `AddHintProvider()` registrations\n- Policy enforcement: Separate `policy_*.go` files (`policy_none.go`, `policy_best_effort.go`, `policy_restricted.go`)\n- Scope handling: `scope_pod.go` for aggregating container hints at pod level\n\n### 3.4 Container Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Entry Points**: `InternalContainerLifecycle` interface (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\nThe container manager provides lifecycle hooks called by the kubelet at key container points:\n\n#### A. Pre-Container Creation: `PreCreateContainer()`\n\nCalled before container creation to configure resource allocation:\n\n```\nPreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 1. CPU Manager: Get CPU assignment\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 cpuSet := cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity(pod.UID, container.Name)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Set in containerConfig.CpusetCpus [cgroup cpuset.cpus]\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. Memory Manager: Get NUMA assignment\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500 numaNodes := memoryManager.GetMemoryAffinity(pod.UID, container.Name)\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 Set in containerConfig.CpusetMems [cgroup cpuset.mems]\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 3. Return updated containerConfig to runtime\n       \u2514\u2500 Runtime creates container with these cpuset constraints\n```\n\n**Implementation**: `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` lines 1-100\n\n**Evidence**:\n- Lines 71-82: CPU Manager integration\n- Lines 83-91: Memory Manager integration\n- Container config populated before runtime call\n\n#### B. Pre-Container Start: `PreStartContainer()`\n\nCalled after container creation but before starting:\n\n```\nPreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 1. CPU Manager: Record container and CPU assignment\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Writes to checkpoint file for recovery\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. Memory Manager: Record container and NUMA assignment\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 memoryManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Writes to checkpoint file for recovery\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 3. Topology Manager: Track container assignment\n       \u2514\u2500 topologyManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n           \u2514\u2500 Updates hint state for future pod admission decisions\n```\n\n#### C. Post-Container Stop: `PostStopContainer()`\n\nCalled after container termination:\n\n```\nPostStopContainer(containerID)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 1. Topology Manager: Clean up container state\n  \u2502    \u2514\u2500 topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 2. CPU Manager: Optional cleanup (state kept for checkpointing)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 3. Memory Manager: Optional cleanup (state kept for checkpointing)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 CPU Manager Failures\n\n**Scenario 1: Static CPU Policy, No Available CPUs**\n\nIf a pod requests exclusive CPUs but all reserved CPUs are exhausted:\n- Static policy cannot find contiguous CPU set\n- `AddContainer()` returns error\n- Pod container startup fails with `CPUManagerError`\n- **Pod remains in Pending state** until CPUs become available\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Resize pod request to non-exclusive CPUs\n- Scale down other exclusive pods\n- Requires manual intervention; no auto-remediation\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Static policy guarantees CPU isolation but can starve pods\n- `none` policy avoids starvation but no CPU affinity\n\n---\n\n**Scenario 2: Reconciliation Lag**\n\nIf a container escapes its assigned cpuset (due to container runtime bug or direct cgroup manipulation):\n- Reconciliation runs every 60s (default)\n- Container consumes CPUs for up to 60 seconds before move\n- **Fairness impact**: One pod can exceed its fair share\n\n**Design Decision**: Trade monitoring frequency for reduced lock contention on container manager\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Memory Manager Failures\n\n**Scenario 1: NUMA Allocation Fails**\n\nIf memory manager cannot allocate memory on preferred NUMA nodes:\n- Static policy rejects the allocation\n- `AddContainer()` returns error\n- Pod cannot start\n\n**Scenario 2: Memory Overcommit**\n\nIf actual pod memory usage exceeds assigned limit:\n- Cgroup OOM killer terminates container\n- **Observed in practice**: BestEffort pods killed first due to OOM score (-999)\n- **Log evidence**: Container killed by OOM killer signal\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Cgroup v2 adds `memory.min` to protect high-priority tiers\n- Adds complexity but improves reliability\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Topology Manager Admission Failures\n\n**Scenario: Topology Affinity Cannot Be Met**\n\nWith `restricted` policy, if CPU/Memory/Device hints have no intersection:\n\n```\nExample:\n  CPU Manager hints: NUMA node 0\n  Memory Manager hints: NUMA node 1\n  Device Manager hints: NUMA node 2\n\n  Intersection: empty\n  Policy: restricted\n  \u2192 Pod REJECTED with TopologyAffinityError\n```\n\n**Impact**: Valid resource requests rejected due to topology constraint mismatch\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use `best-effort` policy to prefer aligned but accept misaligned\n- Adjust pod requests to align with available topology\n- Modify device plugin topology reporting\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- `restricted` prevents performance-hurting misalignment (good for latency-sensitive workloads)\n- `best-effort` allows more schedules but degrades tail latency\n\n---\n\n### 4.4 Resource Quota Enforcement Limits\n\n**Hard Limits** (via CFS quota, memory.max):\n- CPU: Hard cap enforced by kernel CFS scheduler\n- Memory: Hard cap enforced by cgroup OOM killer\n- Cannot be violated; violations cause container termination\n\n**Soft Limits** (via CPU shares, memory.high):\n- CPU shares: Kernel guarantees proportional time, but doesn't hard-cap\n- Memory.high: Kernel reclaims memory via throttling, but allows temporary overage\n\n**Design Limit**: No intermediate guarantees between soft and hard; either pod gets CPU or doesn't\n\n---\n\n### 4.5 Cgroup Version Incompatibility\n\n**Cgroup v1 Issues** (Deprecated):\n- Multiple independent subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, pids)\n- More memory overhead per cgroup\n- Less precise memory accounting\n- **Warning logged** at startup: \"cgroup v1 detected. cgroup v1 support is deprecated...\"\n\n**Cgroup v2 Requirements**:\n- Kernel 5.4+ required for basic support\n- Kernel 5.8+ required for root `cpu.stat` (required for accurate CPU accounting)\n- **Code path**: Lines 52-59 in `container_manager.go` with kernel version checks\n\n**Design Decision**: Support both for backwards compatibility, but strongly encourage v2 migration\n\n---\n\n### 4.6 Platform-Specific Limits\n\n**Linux** (Full support):\n- All managers enabled: CPU, Memory, Topology, Device, DRA\n- Cgroup enforcement via cgroupfs\n\n**Windows** (Minimal support):\n- CPU Manager: Stub (no affinity)\n- Memory Manager: Stub\n- Topology Manager: Stub\n- Device Manager: Basic support only\n- Cgroup: Not available; relies on container runtime limits\n\n**Other Platforms** (Stub):\n- All managers return no-op stubs\n- No resource isolation beyond runtime defaults\n\n---\n\n### 4.7 Node Allocatable Enforcement Tradeoffs\n\n**Enforcement Goal**: Ensure `Node Allocatable = Node Capacity - Reserved`\n\n**Mechanism**:\n- Create cgroup at `kubepods` with resource limits\n- Force all pod cgroups under `kubepods`\n- Periodically enforce limits via cgroup manager updates\n\n**Challenge: Memory Overcommit** (lines 550-558):\n```\nIf actual pod memory usage > allocatable memory:\n  \u251c\u2500 Reduce burstable tier limit (to free memory for guaranteed)\n  \u251c\u2500 If still overcommitted, retry with increased frequency\n  \u2514\u2500 If unresolvable, log error but allow operation\n```\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Strict enforcement can crash workloads (OOM kill)\n- Permissive enforcement allows overcommit (performance degradation)\n- Kubernetes chose permissive: Log but don't kill\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policy Customization\n\n**How to Add New Policy**:\n\n1. **Create policy file**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_custom.go`\n2. **Implement interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(activePodsFunc) error\n    AddContainer(pod, container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(containerID string) error\n    GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    // ... other methods\n}\n```\n3. **Register in NewManager()** (lines 80-100): Add case for policy name\n4. **Implement reconciliation** for crash recovery\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Allocation Deadlock**: If new policy exhausts CPUs, pods pending forever\n- **Data Corruption**: Checkpoint file format must match; incompatible format causes recovery failure\n- **Performance**: Static policy is O(N) search; complex policies could block container startup\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Device Plugin Extension Points\n\n**Device Plugin Registration Flow**:\n\n```\nPlugin Manager watches: /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/\n  \u2514\u2500 Plugin creates Unix socket: example.sock\n      \u2514\u2500 Plugin registers with kubelet via gRPC\n          \u251c\u2500 DevicePluginService.Register(pluginInfo)\n          \u2514\u2500 Passes back: ListAndWatchEndpoint, AllocateEndpoint\n```\n\n**Device Manager Integration**:\n- Location: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`\n- **ListAndWatch gRPC**: Stream device status (healthy/unhealthy)\n- **Allocate gRPC**: Called by container manager to allocate devices\n\n**Topology Hints Support**:\n- Plugin can report NUMA locality for each device\n- Device manager relays to topology manager during hint collection\n- Allows topology-aware device scheduling\n\n**Custom Hook Implementation**:\n```go\n// Device plugin implements\ntype DevicePlugin interface {\n    ListAndWatch(empty *Empty, stream DevicePlugin_ListAndWatchServer) error\n    Allocate(ctx context.Context, request *AllocateRequest) (*AllocateResponse, error)\n    PreStartContainer(ctx context.Context, request *PreStartContainerRequest) (*PreStartContainerResponse, error)\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Allocation Persistence**: Device allocation state lost if kubelet crashes (no checkpoint); devices might be double-allocated\n- **Plugin Crash**: If plugin crashes, allocated devices become orphaned; no auto-recovery\n- **Topology Mismatch**: If plugin reports inconsistent topology across calls, admission decisions become invalid\n\n---\n\n### 5.3 Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Driver Integration\n\n**DRA Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`) provides hooks for custom resource drivers:\n\n```\nResourceClaim with ResourceClassName\n  \u2193\nDRA Manager.PrepareDynamicResources(pod)\n  \u2514\u2500 For each ResourceClaim in pod:\n      \u251c\u2500 Get ResourceDriver endpoint from ResourceClass\n      \u251c\u2500 Call Driver.Prepare(claim) gRPC\n      \u251c\u2500 Wait for ClaimStatus.AllocationResult\n      \u251c\u2500 Return CDI device paths to container runtime\n      \u2514\u2500 Record claim state for unprepare\n```\n\n**Extension**: Resource drivers are fully custom gRPC services (outside kubelet)\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Claim Deadlock**: If driver never completes Prepare(), pod waits forever\n- **Resource Leak**: If driver crashes after Prepare() but before Unprepare(), resources become orphaned\n- **Unavailable Updates**: If driver later reports claim unavailable, kubelet must evict pod; no graceful migration\n\n---\n\n### 5.4 Topology Manager Policy Customization\n\n**How to Add New Policy**:\n\n1. **Create policy file**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_custom.go`\n2. **Implement**:\n```go\ntype TopologyAwarePolicy interface {\n    Name() string\n    CanAdmitPodResult(*TopologyHints) *lifecycle.PodAdmitResult\n    GetTopologyHints(*Pod, *Container) []TopologyHint\n}\n```\n3. **Register in NewManager()**: Add case for policy name\n\n**Builtin Policies** and their characteristics:\n- `none`: Always admits (no affinity enforcement)\n- `best-effort`: Prefers alignment, accepts misalignment \u2192 **Most flexible**\n- `restricted`: Requires alignment \u2192 **Most strict**\n- `single-numa-node`: All containers in pod on single NUMA node \u2192 **Hardware-optimal**\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Starvation**: Overly strict policy might make clusters unschedulable\n- **Inconsistent Hints**: If hint providers disagree (e.g., Device Manager reports different topology than actual), policy enforcement fails\n- **State Corruption**: If topology manager state file corrupted, node becomes unbootable (cannot parse existing pod topology assignments)\n\n---\n\n### 5.5 QoS Reservation Customization\n\n**QoS Reservation Feature** (enabled via `--qos-reserved` flag):\n\n```go\n// Example: reserve 20% of memory for burstable tier\n--qos-reserved=memory=20%\n\n// Translates to:\nQOSReserved: {\n    v1.ResourceMemory: int64(20),\n}\n```\n\n**Mechanism** (in `qos_container_manager_linux.go`, lines 349-373):\n```\nNode Allocatable Memory = 32 GB\nGuaranteed Pods Memory = 10 GB\nQOS Reserved = 20%\n\n\u2192 Burstable Tier Memory Limit = 32 - 10 - (32 * 20%) = 15.6 GB\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Memory Underutilization**: If guaranteed pods never reach reservation, memory wasted\n- **No Enforcement**: This is advisory; burstable pods can still exceed if guaranteed under-utilized\n- **Percentage Interpretation**: Different administrators might interpret percentage differently (of total vs. of allocatable)\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n\n**Exclusive CPU Allocation** (static policy):\n- **Startup Latency**: O(N) search through available CPUs during `AddContainer()` \u2192 **10-50ms for large socket counts**\n- **Checkpoint I/O**: Write to disk on each container addition \u2192 **5-20ms per add**\n- **Reconciliation**: Periodic scan of all containers for escapes \u2192 **100-500ms per 60s cycle**\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use `none` policy if CPU isolation not critical\n- Increase reconciliation interval if I/O pressure high\n- Pre-reserve CPU sets to avoid fragmentation\n\n#### Memory Manager Overhead\n\n**NUMA Affinity Calculation** (static policy):\n- **Startup Latency**: Lookup NUMA topology and find compatible nodes \u2192 **5-20ms**\n- **Checkpoint I/O**: Write allocation state \u2192 **5-20ms**\n\n**Memory QoS** (cgroup v2):\n- **Per-Tier Updates**: Calculate and apply memory limits every 60s \u2192 **10-50ms per update**\n- **Additional Syscalls**: Setting memory.min, memory.high per-pod \u2192 Linear with pod count\n\n#### Topology Manager Latency\n\n**Hint Collection**:\n- For each pod, call GetTopologyHints() on all hint providers (CPU, Memory, Device managers)\n- With 3 managers, each taking 5-10ms \u2192 **Total 15-30ms per pod admission**\n- Serialized (not parallel), so scales linearly with managers\n\n**Policy Evaluation**:\n- best-effort/restricted: Intersection of NUMA node sets \u2192 **O(N*M) with N hints, M managers**\n- single-numa-node: Stricter evaluation \u2192 **O(N\u00b2) in worst case**\n\n#### Device Manager Latency\n\n**Device Allocation**:\n- gRPC call to device plugin `Allocate()` \u2192 **50-500ms depending on plugin implementation**\n- Plugin might contact external hardware \u2192 Additional latency\n\n**Critical Path**: Device plugin latency is on critical path for container startup\n\n---\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Failure Recovery\n\n#### Checkpoint-Based Recovery\n\n**CPU Manager Checkpoint** (`cpu_manager_state` file):\n```\nLocation: <kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state\nFormat: JSON with container ID \u2192 CPUSet mapping\nPurpose: Recover allocations after kubelet crash\nLimitations: Cannot recover allocations for containers deleted before kubelet restart\n```\n\n**Recovery Process**:\n1. On start, load checkpoint\n2. Query runtime for running containers\n3. For each running container:\n   - If in checkpoint, restore CPU affinity\n   - If not in checkpoint, **reset cpuset to all CPUs** (loss of exclusive allocation)\n4. Reconcile every 60s to restore any escaped processes\n\n**Risk**: If checkpoint corrupted or lost, all exclusive CPU allocations forgotten\n\n---\n\n#### Device Plugin State Loss\n\n**No Checkpoint for Device Allocation**:\n- Device allocation state kept in memory\n- On kubelet crash, state lost\n- **Devices might be double-allocated if pod scheduled to another node**\n- **Design tradeoff**: Avoid I/O overhead for device state at cost of recovery safety\n\n**Mitigation**: External resource management (e.g., k8s resource reservations) should enforce uniqueness\n\n---\n\n#### Topology Manager State Loss\n\n**No Persistent State**:\n- Topology assignments kept in memory\n- On restart, all pods re-admitted via Admit() method\n- **Design decision**: Stateless readmission safer than corrupt state recovery\n- **Cost**: Admits only pods that currently exist (not past decisions)\n\n---\n\n### 6.3 Observability and Debugging\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**CPU Manager** (prometheus):\n- No official metrics (state internal)\n- **Observable via cgroups**: `cat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/cpuset.cpus`\n\n**Memory Manager**:\n- No official metrics\n- **Observable via cgroups**: `cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/memory.usage_in_bytes`\n\n**Topology Manager**:\n- No official metrics\n- **Observable via logs**: \"Successfully admitted pod for topology policy\"\n\n**Device Manager**:\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_allocation_duration_seconds` histogram\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_request_total` counter\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_request_errors_total` counter\n\n#### Logging Evidence\n\n**CPU Manager Debug Logs** (`--v=4` or higher):\n```\n\"Container X has pinned cpus\"\n\"Successfully added container X to exclusive cpus\"\n\"Reconciling container assignments\"\n```\n\n**QoS Manager Logs**:\n```\n\"Updated QOS container cpushares\"\n\"Setting memory reserved\"\n\"MemoryQoS config for pod\"\n```\n\n**Topology Manager Logs**:\n```\n\"Successfully admitted pod for topology policy\"\n\"Pod rejected for topology policy: TopologyAffinityError\"\n```\n\n---\n\n#### Debugging Cgroups\n\n**Check pod cgroup hierarchy**:\n```bash\n# Guaranteed pod\nls /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.guaranteed.podXXX/\n\n# Burstable pod\nls /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/\n\n# View CPU set\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/cpuset.cpus\n\n# View memory limit\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/memory.limit_in_bytes\n```\n\n**Check QoS tier limits**:\n```bash\n# Burstable tier CPU shares\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/kubepods.burstable/cpu.shares\n\n# BestEffort tier\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/kubepods.besteffort/cpu.shares\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6.4 Node Allocatable Enforcement\n\n**Default Reservations**:\n- `kube-reserved`: CPU and memory reserved for kubelet, systemd, etc. (default none)\n- `system-reserved`: CPU and memory reserved for OS (default none)\n- `eviction-hard`: Thresholds for evicting pods (e.g., memory < 5%)\n\n**Effective Node Allocatable**:\n```\nAllocatable = Capacity - Kube-Reserved - System-Reserved\n```\n\n**Example**:\n```\nNode Capacity:     32 CPUs, 64 GB memory\nKube-Reserved:     2 CPUs, 4 GB memory\nSystem-Reserved:   1 CPU, 2 GB memory\n\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\nNode Allocatable:  29 CPUs, 58 GB memory (reported to scheduler)\n```\n\n**Enforcement Mechanism** (lines 550-558 in `container_manager_linux.go`):\n- Root pod cgroup (`kubepods`) created with limits = allocatable\n- All user pods placed under `kubepods`\n- Periodic enforcement every 60s\n\n**Failure Scenario**: If actual pod usage > allocatable:\n- Memory OOM killer activates\n- BestEffort pods killed first (OOM score -999)\n- Guaranteed pods protected (OOM score 0 with systemd driver)\n- **Design decision**: Accept temporary overages rather than preemptively kill\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Important Files and Directories Map\n\n### Core Container Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` - Main ContainerManager interface definition\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` - Linux implementation with initialization and node setup\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` - Windows stub implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` - CgroupManager, regardless of individual pod lifecycle\n- **Device Manager as Bridge**: Translates plugin gRPC into kubelet resource constraints\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a complex, multi-faceted subsystem that orchestrates resource allocation and enforcement across Linux cgroups, device plugins, and custom resource drivers. Its architecture achieves separation of concerns (CPU, Memory, Devices managed independently) while enforcing global constraints (topology affinity via topology manager, QoS fairness via QoS tiers). The tradeoffs between strict enforcement and operational flexibility, between comprehensive monitoring and performance, are consciously designed to prioritize pod stability over perfect fairness\u2014a pragmatic choice for a diverse, multi-tenant platform.\n",
